style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.btplc.com">www<wbr />.btplc<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>BT Group plc</b> (<a href="/wiki/Doing_business_as" class="mw-redirect" title="Doing business as">trading as</a> <b>BT</b> and formerly <b>British Telecom</b>) is a British <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunications</a> <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. It has operations in around 180 countries and is the largest provider of <a href="/wiki/Landline" title="Landline">fixed-line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_access" title="Internet access">broadband</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_telephony" title="Mobile telephony">mobile</a> services in the UK, and also provides <a href="/wiki/Pay_television" title="Pay television">subscription television</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">IT services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BT\'s origins date back to the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Electric_Telegraph_Company" title="Electric Telegraph Company">Electric Telegraph Company</a> in 1846 which developed a nationwide communications network. In 1912, the <a href="/wiki/General_Post_Office" title="General Post Office">General Post Office</a>, a government department, became the monopoly telecoms supplier in the United Kingdom. The Post Office Act of 1969 led to the GPO becoming a public corporation. British Telecommunications, trading as <i>British Telecom</i>, was formed in 1980, and became independent of the Post Office in 1981. British Telecommunications was privatised in 1984, becoming <i>British Telecommunications plc</i>, with some 50 percent of its shares sold to investors. The Government sold its remaining stake in further share sales in 1991 and 1993. BT is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Royal_Warrant_holders_of_the_British_Royal_Family" title="List of Royal Warrant holders of the British Royal Family">Royal Warrant holder of the British Royal Family</a> and has a primary listing on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>, a secondary listing on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>, and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100_Index" title="FTSE 100 Index">FTSE 100 Index</a>.\n</p><p>BT controls a number of large subsidiaries. <a href="/wiki/BT_Global_Services" title="BT Global Services">BT Global Services</a> division supplies telecoms services to corporate and government customers worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and its <a href="/wiki/BT_Consumer" title="BT Consumer">BT Consumer</a> division supplies <a href="/wiki/Telephony" title="Telephony">telephony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_access" title="Internet access">broadband</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pay_television" title="Pay television">subscription television</a> services in Great Britain to around 18&#160;million customers.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In January 2016, BT acquired <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a> for \xc2\xa312.5 billion.\n</p>\n<div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#1878_to_1969"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">1878 to 1969</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-3"><a href="#Public_corporation"><span class="tocnumber">1.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Public corporation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#1970_to_1990"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">1970 to 1990</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#1991_to_2006"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">1991 to 2006</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#2007_to_2012"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">2007 to 2012</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#2013_to_present"><span class="tocnumber">1.5</span> <span class="toctext">2013 to present</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Operations"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Operations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Corporate_affairs"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Corporate affairs</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Buildings_and_facilities"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Buildings and facilities</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#Headquarters"><span class="tocnumber">3.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Headquarters</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12"><a href="#Buildings_and_stations"><span class="tocnumber">3.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Buildings and stations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13"><a href="#Telecommunications_towers"><span class="tocnumber">3.1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Telecommunications towers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-14"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">3.1.4</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Divisions"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Divisions</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#Customer_facing"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Customer facing</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#Internal_service_unit"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Internal service unit</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Corporate_governance"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Corporate governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Pension_fund"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Pension fund</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Sponsorships"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Sponsorships</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Historical_financial_performance"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Historical financial performance</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#2008\xe2\x80\x93present"><span class="tocnumber">3.6.1</span> <span class="toctext">2008\xe2\x80\x93present</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23"><a href="#1992\xe2\x80\x932007"><span class="tocnumber">3.6.2</span> <span class="toctext">1992\xe2\x80\x932007</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Environmental_record"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Environmental record</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Controversies"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Controversies</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#World_Wide_Web_hyperlink_patent"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">World Wide Web hyperlink patent</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Behavioural_targeting"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Behavioural targeting</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Huawei_infrastructure_access"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Huawei infrastructure access</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Alleged_complicity_with_drone_strikes_in_Yemen_and_Somalia"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Alleged complicity with drone strikes in Yemen and Somalia</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Advert" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>contains content that is written like <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_soapbox_or_means_of_promotion" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">an advertisement</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by removing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Spam" title="Wikipedia:Spam">promotional content</a> and inappropriate <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">external links</a>, and by adding encyclopedic content written from a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutral point of view</a>.</span>  <small><i>(October 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>BT\'s origins date back to the establishment of the first telecommunications companies in Britain.  Among them was the first commercial <a href="/wiki/Telegraphy" title="Telegraphy">telegraph service</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Electric_Telegraph_Company" title="Electric Telegraph Company">Electric Telegraph Company</a>, established in 1846. As these companies amalgamated and were taken over or collapsed, the remaining companies were transferred to <a href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Government-owned corporation">state control</a> under the <a href="/wiki/General_Post_Office" title="General Post Office">Post Office</a> in 1912. These companies were merged and <a href="/wiki/Rebranding" title="Rebranding">rebranded</a> as British Telecom.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1878_to_1969">1878 to 1969</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1878 to 1969">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_Tower-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/BT_Tower-1.jpg/220px-BT_Tower-1.jpg" width="220" height="357" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/BT_Tower-1.jpg/330px-BT_Tower-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/BT_Tower-1.jpg/440px-BT_Tower-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2163" data-file-height="3510" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_Tower-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/BT_Tower" title="BT Tower">BT Tower</a>, originally the Post Office Tower, completed 1964</div></div></div>\n<p>In  1878 <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graham_Bell" title="Alexander Graham Bell">Alexander Graham Bell</a> demonstrated his recently developed telephone to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> at <a href="/wiki/Osborne_House" title="Osborne House">Osborne House</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Linge_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Linge-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> A few days later the first telephone in Britain was installed, under licence from the General Post Office, by engineers from David Moseley and Sons,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (September 2018)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to connect the <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> premises of  hardware merchant John Hudson with his other premises in nearby <a href="/wiki/Shudehill" class="mw-redirect" title="Shudehill">Shudehill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Linge_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Linge-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>  The first telephone exchange, allowing any of an area\'s phones to be connected with any other, was opened in London in August 1879, soon followed by one in Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-Linge_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Linge-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> From 1878 on, telephone service in Britain was provided by private companies such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Telephone_Company" title="National Telephone Company">National Telephone Company</a>. In 1896, the National Telephone Company was taken over by the General Post Office. In 1912 it became the primary supplier of telecommunications services, after the Post Office took over the private telephone service in Britain, except for a few local authority services.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_corporation">Public corporation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Public corporation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Converting the Post Office into a nationalised industry, as opposed to a governmental department, was first discussed in 1932; a report on the subject<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (September 2018)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that year was rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 1961, more proposals were ignored. <sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 October 1969, under the Post Office Act of 1969, the Post Office ceased to be a government department and it became established as a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public corporation</a>. The Act gave the Post Office the exclusive privilege of operating telecommunications systems with listed powers to authorise others to run such systems. Effectively, the General Post Office retained its telecommunications monopoly.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970_to_1990">1970 to 1990</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970 to 1990">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Telecom_1981.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/British_Telecom_1981.svg/150px-British_Telecom_1981.svg.png" width="150" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/British_Telecom_1981.svg/225px-British_Telecom_1981.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/British_Telecom_1981.svg/300px-British_Telecom_1981.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="461" data-file-height="465" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Telecom_1981.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo used from 1980 to 1991</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1977, the Carter Committee Report recommended a further division of the two main services and for their relocation under two individual corporations. The findings contained in the report led to the renaming of <a href="/wiki/Post_Office_Telecommunications" title="Post Office Telecommunications">Post Office Telecommunications</a> as British Telecommunications (trading as British Telecom) in 1980, although it remained part of the Post Office.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Telecommunications_Act_1981" title="British Telecommunications Act 1981">British Telecommunications Act 1981</a> transferred the responsibility for telecommunications services from the Post Office, creating two separate corporations, <a href="/wiki/Post_Office_Ltd" title="Post Office Ltd">Post Office Ltd</a> and British Telecommunications. At this time the first steps were taken to introduce competition into British telecommunications industry. In particular, the Act empowered the Secretary of State for Trade and Industry, as well as British Telecommunications, to license other operators to run public telecommunications systems. Additionally, a framework was established which enabled the Secretary of State to set standards with the <a href="/wiki/British_Standards_Institution" class="mw-redirect" title="British Standards Institution">British Standards Institution</a> (BSI) for apparatus supplied to the public by third parties, and had the effect of requiring British Telecommunications to connect approved apparatus to its systems. The Secretary of State made use of these new powers and began the process of opening up the apparatus supply market, where a phased programme of liberalisation was started in 1981. In 1982, a licence was granted to Cable &amp; Wireless to run a public telecommunications network through its subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Communications_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercury Communications Ltd">Mercury Communications Ltd</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 July 1982, the Government formally announced its intention to privatise British Telecommunications with the sale of up to 51% of the company\'s shares to private investors. This intention was confirmed by the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_Act_1984" title="Telecommunications Act 1984">Telecommunications Act 1984</a>, which received Royal Assent on 12 April that year. The transfer to British Telecommunications plc of the business of British Telecommunications, the statutory corporation, took place on 6 August 1984 and, on 20 November 1984, more than 50 per cent of British Telecommunications shares were sold to the public. At the time, this was the largest share issue in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The new legislation was intended to enable British Telecommunications to become more responsive to competition in GB and to expand its operations globally. Commercial freedom granted to British Telecommunications allowed it to enter into new joint ventures and, if it so decided, to engage in the manufacture of its own apparatus. The company\'s transfer into the private sector continued in December 1991 when the Government sold around half its remaining holding of 47.6% of shares, reducing its stake to 21.8%. Substantially all the government\'s remaining shares were sold in a third flotation in July 1993, raising \xc2\xa35&#160;billion for the Treasury and introducing 750,000 new shareholders to the company.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1984 Act also abolished British Telecommunications\'s exclusive privilege of running telecommunications systems and established a framework to safeguard the workings of competition. This meant that British Telecommunications finally lost its monopoly in running telecommunications systems, which it had technically retained under the 1981 Act despite the Secretary of State\'s licensing powers. It now required a licence in the same way as any other telecommunications operator. The principal licence granted to British Telecommunications laid down strict and extensive conditions affecting the range of its activities, including those of manufacture and supply of apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1985, <a href="/wiki/Cellnet" class="mw-redirect" title="Cellnet">Cellnet</a> was launched as a subsidiary of Telecom Securicor Cellular Radio Limited, a 60:40 venture between British Telecommunications and <a href="/wiki/G4S" title="G4S">Securicor</a> respectively. Securicor originally invested \xc2\xa34&#160;million in Cellnet in 1983. In 1999, BT purchased Securicor\'s shares in Cellnet for \xc2\xa33.15&#160;billion. The company was later rebranded as BT Cellnet, and became a part of BT Wireless, a group of subsidiary companies owned by BT.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The next major development for British Telecommunications, and a move towards a more open market in telecommunications, occurred in 1991. On 5 March, the Government\'s <a href="/wiki/White_Paper" class="mw-redirect" title="White Paper">White Paper</a>, "Competition and Choice: Telecommunications Policy" for the 1990s, was issued. In effect, it ended the duopoly which had been shared by British Telecommunications and <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Communications" title="Mercury Communications">Mercury Communications</a> in the UK since November 1983 and the build-up to privatisation. The new policy enabled customers to acquire telecommunications services from competing providers using a variety of technologies. Independent "retail" companies were permitted to bulk-buy telecommunications capacity and sell it in packages to business and domestic users. The White Paper was endorsed by British Telecommunications, the new policy enabling the company to compete freely and more effectively by offering flexible pricing packages to meet the needs of different types of customer.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1991_to_2006">1991 to 2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1991 to 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_old_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4f/BT_old_logo.svg/150px-BT_old_logo.svg.png" width="150" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4f/BT_old_logo.svg/225px-BT_old_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4f/BT_old_logo.svg/300px-BT_old_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="234" data-file-height="163" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_old_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The BT brand and piper logo were introduced in 1991. The logo remained until 2003.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 2 April 1991, the company started using a new trading name, BT, and new branding.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 1994, BT and <a href="/wiki/MCI_Communications" title="MCI Communications">MCI Communication Corporation</a>, the second largest carrier of long distance telecommunications services in the United States, launched <a href="/wiki/Concert_Communications_Services" title="Concert Communications Services">Concert Communications Services</a>, a $1&#160;billion joint venture company. This alliance gave BT and MCI a global network for providing end-to-end connectivity for advanced business services. Concert was the first company to provide a single-source broad portfolio of global communications services for multinational customers. On 3 November 1996, BT and MCI announced they had entered into a merger agreement to create a global telecommunications company called Concert plc, to be incorporated in GB, with headquarters in both <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> As part of the alliance BT acquired a 20% holding in MCI. Nevertheless, following US carrier <a href="/wiki/WorldCom" class="mw-redirect" title="WorldCom">WorldCom</a>\'s rival bid for MCI on 1 October 1997, BT ultimately decided in November, to sell its stake in MCI to WorldCom for $7&#160;billion. The deal with WorldCom resulted in a profit of more than $2&#160;billion on BT\'s original investment in MCI, with an additional $465&#160;million severance fee for the break-up of the proposed merger.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2000, following modifications to BT\'s licence in April 2000, BT offered <a href="/wiki/Local_loop_unbundling" class="mw-redirect" title="Local loop unbundling">local loop unbundling</a> (LLU) to other telecommunications operators, enabling them to use BT\'s copper local loops (the connection between the customer\'s premises and the exchange) to connect directly with their customers.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_(Spain)_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_%28Spain%29_01.jpg/220px-British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_%28Spain%29_01.jpg" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_%28Spain%29_01.jpg/330px-British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_%28Spain%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_%28Spain%29_01.jpg/440px-British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_%28Spain%29_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2351" data-file-height="2205" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Telecom_offices_in_Madrid_(Spain)_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BT offices in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Dot_com_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="Dot com crash">dot com crash</a>, the group undertook a board restructuring and asset sale to address its large debts. In May 2001, BT announced a three-for-ten rights issue to raise \xc2\xa35.9&#160;billion\xe2\x80\x94still GB\'s largest ever rights issue\xe2\x80\x94and the sale of <a href="/wiki/Yell_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Yell Group">Yell Group</a>, the international directories and associated e-commerce business, for \xc2\xa32.14&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Both activities were completed in June 2001. The group also sold some of its property portfolio to <a href="/wiki/Telereal_Trillium" title="Telereal Trillium">Telereal Trillium</a>, a property company.<sup id="cite_ref-TelerealTrillium_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TelerealTrillium-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BT renamed its BT Wireless division as <a href="/wiki/O2_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="O2 (United Kingdom)">O2</a> in September 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and confirmed it planned to demerge the unit in November that year. Shareholders approved the demerger at an <a href="/wiki/Extraordinary_general_meeting" title="Extraordinary general meeting">extraordinary general meeting</a> held in Birmingham in October 2001, with 4.297&#160;billion British Telecommunications shares voted in favour, and 0.67&#160;million voted against.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> BT Wireless demerged in 2001, and was relaunched on 18 June 2002 as O2. O2 was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica" title="Telef\xc3\xb3nica">Telef\xc3\xb3nica</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2003, BT unveiled its current corporate identity, known as the "Connected World", and brand values.<sup id="cite_ref-indep8403_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indep8403-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Reflecting the aspirations of a technologically innovative future, the connected world is designed to embody BT\'s five corporate values: trustworthy, helpful, inspiring, straightforward, heart. The globe device part of the logo was originally designed by the <a href="/wiki/Wolff_Olins" title="Wolff Olins">Wolff Olins</a> brand consultancy for BT\'s <a href="/wiki/Concert_Communications_Services" title="Concert Communications Services">Concert</a> joint venture with <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Corporation" title="AT&amp;T Corporation">AT&amp;T</a>, and was subsequently used by BT\'s internet division, Openworld, prior to being adopted by the company as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-indep8403_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indep8403-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Communications Act, 2003, which came into force on 25 July 2003, introduced a new industry regulator, the Office of Communications (<a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a>), to replace the Office of Telecommunications (<a href="/wiki/Oftel" title="Oftel">Oftel</a>). It also introduced a new regulatory framework. The licensing regime was replaced by a general authorisation for companies to provide telecommunications services subject to general conditions of entitlement and, in some instances, specific conditions. Under a specific condition BT retained its universal service obligation (USO) for GB, excluding the Hull area. The USO included connecting consumers to the fixed telephone network, schemes for consumers with special social needs, and the provision of call box services.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_History_6-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_History-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the summer of 2004, BT launched Consult 21, an industry consultation for BT\'s 21st century network (21CN) programme. <a href="/wiki/21CN" class="mw-redirect" title="21CN">21CN</a> is a next-generation network transformation, that, at one time, was due for completion by the end of 2010. Using internet protocol technology, 21CN will replace the existing networks and communications from any device such as mobile phone, PC, PDA, or home phone, to any other device.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004, BT was awarded the contract to deliver and manage N3, a secure and fast broadband network for the <a href="/wiki/NHS_National_Programme_for_IT" class="mw-redirect" title="NHS National Programme for IT">NHS National Programme for IT</a> (NPfIT) program, on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/English_National_Health_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="English National Health Service">English National Health Service</a> (NHS).<sup id="cite_ref-BT_2010_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_2010-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005 BT made a number of important<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> acquisitions. In February 2005, BT acquired Infonet (now re-branded BT Infonet), a large telecoms company based in <a href="/wiki/El_Segundo,_California" title="El Segundo, California">El Segundo, California</a>, giving BT access to new geographies. It also acquired the second largest telecoms operator in the Italian business market, Albacom. Then in April 2005, it bought Radianz from Reuters (now rebranded as BT Radianz), which expanded BT\'s coverage and provided BT with more buying power in certain countries.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2006, BT acquired online electrical retailer <a href="/wiki/Dabs.com" title="Dabs.com">Dabs.com</a> for \xc2\xa330.6&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/BT_Home_Hub" class="mw-redirect" title="BT Home Hub">BT Home Hub</a> manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Inventel" title="Inventel">Inventel</a> was also launched in June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2006, BT confirmed that it would be investing 75% of its total capital spending, put at \xc2\xa310&#160;billion over five years, in its new <a href="/wiki/Internet_Protocol" title="Internet Protocol">Internet Protocol</a> (IP) based <a href="/wiki/BT_21CN" title="BT 21CN">21st century network</a> (21CN). Annual savings of \xc2\xa31&#160;billion per annum were expected when the transition to the new network was to have been completed in 2010, with over 50% of its customers to have been transferred by 2008. (For actual progress see <a href="/wiki/BT_21CN" title="BT 21CN">BT 21CN</a>). That month the first customers on to 21CN was successfully tested at <a href="/wiki/Adastral_Park" title="Adastral Park">Adastral Park</a> in Suffolk.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_to_2012">2007 to 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2007 to 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In January 2007, BT acquired Sheffield-based ISP, <a href="/wiki/PlusNet" class="mw-redirect" title="PlusNet">PlusNet</a> plc, adding 200,000 customers. BT stated that PlusNet will continue to operate separately out of its Sheffield head-office.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 1 February 2007, BT announced agreed terms to acquire <a href="/wiki/International_Network_Services_Inc." title="International Network Services Inc.">International Network Services Inc.</a> (INS), an international provider of IT consultancy and software.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2007, Sir <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rake" title="Michael Rake">Michael Rake</a> succeeded Sir Christopher Bland.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In April that year, they acquired <a href="/wiki/COMSAT" title="COMSAT">COMSAT International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> followed in October by the acquisition of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lynx_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lynx Technology (page does not exist)">Lynx Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BT acquired Wire One Communications in June 2008 and folded the company into "BT Conferencing", its existing conferencing unit, as a new video business unit<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\nIn July 2008, BT acquired the online business directory firm Ufindus for \xc2\xa320 million in order to expand its position in the local information market in GB.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On 28 July 2008, BT acquired <a href="/wiki/Ribbit_(telecommunications_company)" title="Ribbit (telecommunications company)">Ribbit</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">Mountain View, California</a>, "Silicon Valley\'s First Phone Company". Ribbit provides <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a>/<a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flex" class="mw-redirect" title="Adobe Flex">Flex</a> APIs, allowing web developers to incorporate telephony features into their <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">software as a service</a> (SaaS) applications.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early days of its fibre broadband rollout, BT said it would deliver fibre-to-the-premises (<a href="/wiki/FTTP" class="mw-redirect" title="FTTP">FTTP</a>) to around 25% of the Country, with the rest catered for by the slower fibre-to-the-cabinet (FTTC), which uses copper wiring to deliver the final stretch of the connection. In 2014, with less than 0.7% of the company\'s fibre network being FTTP, BT dropped the 25% target, saying that it was "far less relevant today" because of improvements made to the headline speed of FTTC, which had doubled to 80Mbit/s since its fibre broadband rollout was first announced.<sup id="cite_ref-alphr.com_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alphr.com-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> To supplement FTTC, BT offered an \'FTTP on Demand\' product.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In January 2015, BT stopped taking orders for the on-demand product.<sup id="cite_ref-ispreview.co.uk_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ispreview.co.uk-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 April 2009, BT Engage IT was created from the merger of two previous BT acquisitions, Lynx Technology and Basilica. Apart from the name change not much else changed in operations for another 12 months.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On 14 May 2009, BT said it was cutting up to 15,000 jobs in the coming year after it announced its results for the year to 31 March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Then in July 2009, BT offered workers a long holiday for an up front sum of 25% of their annual wage or a one-off payment of \xc2\xa31000 if they agree to go part-time.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 April 2011, BT launched the first online <a href="/wiki/Not-for-profit" class="mw-redirect" title="Not-for-profit">not-for-profit</a> fundraising service for <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a> charities called <a href="/wiki/BT_MyDonate" title="BT MyDonate">BT MyDonate</a> as part of its investment to the community. The service will pass on 100% of all donations made through the site to the charity, and unlike <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_online_charity_donation_services_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Comparison of online charity donation services in the United Kingdom">other services</a> which take a proportion as commission and charge charities for using their services, BT will only pass on credit/debit card charges for each donation. The service allows people to register to give money to charity or collect fundraising donations. BT developed MyDonate with the support of <a href="/wiki/Cancer_Research_UK" title="Cancer Research UK">Cancer Research UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Changing_Faces_(charity)" title="Changing Faces (charity)">Changing Faces</a>, <a href="/wiki/KidsOut" title="KidsOut">KidsOut</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Society_for_the_Prevention_of_Cruelty_to_Children" title="National Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Children">NSPCC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Aid_Federation_of_England" title="Women&#39;s Aid Federation of England">Women\'s Aid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_to_present">2013 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In March 2013, BT was allocated 4G spectrum in the UK following an auction and assignment by Ofcom, after paying \xc2\xa3201.5m.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 August 2013, BT launched its first television channels, <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a>, to compete with rival broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Plans for the channels\' launch came about when it was announced in June 2012 that BT had been awarded a package of broadcast rights for the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> from the 2013\xe2\x80\x9314 to 2015\xe2\x80\x9316 season, broadcasting 38 matches from each season.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In February 2013, BT acquired <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Inc." title="ESPN Inc.">ESPN Inc.</a>\'s UK and Ireland TV channels, continuing its expansion into sports broadcasting.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN_America" title="ESPN America">ESPN America</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Classic_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPN Classic (UK)">ESPN Classic</a> were both closed, while <a href="/wiki/ESPN_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPN (UK)">ESPN</a> continued to be operated by BT. On 9 November 2013, BT announced it had acquired exclusive rights to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europa_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Europa League">Europa League</a> for \xc2\xa3897m, from the 2015 season, with some free games remaining including both finals.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 November 2014, BT created a new central business services (CBS) organisation to provide customer services and improve operational efficiency levels.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 November 2014, shares in BT rose considerably on the announcement that the company was in talks to buy back <a href="/wiki/O2_(UK)" title="O2 (UK)">O2</a>, while at the same time confirmed it was also in talks to acquire <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> BT subsequently entered into exclusive talks to buy EE for \xc2\xa312.5 billion on 15 December 2014<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and confirmed on 5 February 2015, subject to regulatory approval. The deal will combine BT\'s 10 million retail customers and EE\'s 24.5 million direct mobile subscribers. <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a> will own 12% of BT, while <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">Orange S.A.</a> will own 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2015, launched a 4G service as <a href="/wiki/BT_Mobile" title="BT Mobile">BT Mobile</a><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> BT Group CEO <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Patterson" title="Gavin Patterson">Gavin Patterson</a> announced that BT plans to migrate all of its customers onto the IP network by 2025, switching off the company\'s <a href="/wiki/ISDN" class="mw-redirect" title="ISDN">ISDN</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 January 2016, BT received final unconditional approval by the <a href="/wiki/Competition_and_Markets_Authority" title="Competition and Markets Authority">Competition and Markets Authority</a> to acquire <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The deal was officially completed on 29 January 2016 with <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a> now owning 12% of BT, while <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">Orange S.A.</a> own 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 February 2016, BT announced a new organisational structure that will take effect from April 2016 following the successful acquisition of <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a>. The EE brand, network and high street stores will be retained and will become a second consumer division, operating alongside <a href="/wiki/BT_Consumer" title="BT Consumer">BT Consumer</a>. It will serve customers with mobile services, broadband and TV and will continue to deliver the Emergency Services Network contract which was awarded to EE in late 2015. There will be a new BT Business and Public Sector division that will have around \xc2\xa35bn of revenues and will serve small and large businesses as well as the public sector in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>. It will comprise the existing <a href="/wiki/BT_Business" class="mw-redirect" title="BT Business">BT Business</a> division along with EE\'s business division and those parts of <a href="/wiki/BT_Global_Services" title="BT Global Services">BT Global Services</a> that are UK focused. There will also be another new division; BT Wholesale and Ventures that will comprise the existing <a href="/wiki/BT_Wholesale" class="mw-redirect" title="BT Wholesale">BT Wholesale</a> division along with EE\'s <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virtual_network_operator" title="Mobile virtual network operator">MVNO</a> business as well as some specialist businesses such as Fleet, Payphones and Directories. Gerry McQuade, currently Chief Sales and Marketing Officer, Business at EE, will be its CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 June 2017, BT appointed <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a> as its new auditor to replace <a href="/wiki/PwC" class="mw-redirect" title="PwC">PwC</a> in the wake of the fraud scandal in Italy that triggered a major profit warning earlier this year.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In last April, KPMG fired six US employees over a scandal that calls into question efforts to ensure that public company accounts are being properly scrutinised.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 July 2017, <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a> reported that BT "has called in consultants from <a href="/wiki/McKinsey" class="mw-redirect" title="McKinsey">McKinsey</a> to conduct a review of its businesses in the hope of saving hundreds of millions of pounds per year. The work, dubbed \'Project Novator\', is understood to include a potential merger of BT\xe2\x80\x99s struggling global services corporate networking and IT unit with its business and public sector division".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 July 2017, BT announced organisational changes to "simplify its operating model, strengthen accountabilities and accelerate its transformation" and involves bringing together its <a href="/wiki/BT_Consumer" title="BT Consumer">BT Consumer</a> and <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a> divisions into a new unified BT Consumer division that will operate across three brands \xe2\x80\x93 BT, EE and <a href="/wiki/Plusnet" title="Plusnet">Plusnet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> It will take effect from 1 April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 April 2018, BT announced further organisational changes following unification of its BT Consumer and EE divisions, and involves bringing together its <a href="/wiki/BT_Business_and_Public_Sector" title="BT Business and Public Sector">BT Business and Public Sector</a> and <a href="/wiki/BT_Wholesale_and_Ventures" title="BT Wholesale and Ventures">BT Wholesale and Ventures</a> divisions into a new unified division known as <i>BT Enterprise</i>. It will also include BT\'s Ventures business which "acts as an incubator for potential new growth areas of the company" and will report as a single unit from 1 October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_Adastral_Park,_Ipswich,_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/BT_Adastral_Park%2C_Ipswich%2C_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg/220px-BT_Adastral_Park%2C_Ipswich%2C_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/BT_Adastral_Park%2C_Ipswich%2C_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg/330px-BT_Adastral_Park%2C_Ipswich%2C_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/BT_Adastral_Park%2C_Ipswich%2C_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg/440px-BT_Adastral_Park%2C_Ipswich%2C_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_Adastral_Park,_Ipswich,_UK_-_geograph.org.uk_-_39100.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Adastral_Park" title="Adastral Park">Adastral Park</a> campus at <a href="/wiki/Martlesham_Heath" title="Martlesham Heath">Martlesham Heath</a> in Suffolk, the principal site of <a href="/wiki/BT_Research" title="BT Research">BT Research</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>BT Group is a <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a>; the majority of its businesses and assets are held by its wholly owned subsidiary British Telecommunications plc.<sup id="cite_ref-Groupbusinesses_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Groupbusinesses-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> BT\'s businesses are operated under special government regulation by the British telecoms regulator <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Oftel" title="Oftel">Oftel</a>). BT has been found to have significant market power in some markets following market reviews by Ofcom. In these markets, BT is required to comply with additional obligations such as meeting reasonable requests to supply services and not to discriminate.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BT runs the <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange" title="Telephone exchange">telephone exchanges</a>, trunk network and <a href="/wiki/Local_loop" title="Local loop">local loop</a> connections for the vast majority of British fixed-line telephones. Currently BT is responsible for approximately 28&#160;million telephone lines in GB. Apart from <a href="/wiki/KCOM_Group" title="KCOM Group">KCOM Group</a>, which serves Kingston upon Hull, BT is the only UK telecoms operator to have a <i><a href="/wiki/Universal_service" title="Universal service">Universal Service Obligation</a>,</i> (USO) which means it must provide a fixed telephone line to any address in the UK. It is also obliged to provide public call boxes.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As well as continuing to provide service in those traditional areas in which BT has an obligation to provide services or is closely regulated, BT has expanded into more profitable products and services where there is less regulation. These are principally, broadband internet service and <a href="/wiki/Bespoke" title="Bespoke">bespoke</a> solutions in telecommunications and information technology.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buildings_and_facilities">Buildings and facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Buildings and facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:British_Telecom_buildings_and_structures" title="Category:British Telecom buildings and structures">Category:British Telecom buildings and structures</a></div>\n<p>As BT operates in around 180 countries, it <a href="/wiki/Ownership" title="Ownership">owns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lease" title="Lease">leases</a> a range of <a href="/wiki/Building" title="Building">buildings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_facility" title="Telecommunications facility">facilities</a> in the UK and around the world. In 2001, it sold some of its UK property portfolio for \xc2\xa32.38 billion to <a href="/wiki/Telereal_Trillium" title="Telereal Trillium">Telereal Trillium</a> in a 30-year <a href="/wiki/Leaseback" title="Leaseback">leaseback</a>. The deal included 6,700 properties and contributed towards alleviating its debt at the time, with the main advantage being flexibility as it allows BT to vacate property over time, so as to adapt to changing operational requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-TelerealTrillium_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TelerealTrillium-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Headquarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg/220px-BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg/330px-BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg/440px-BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2512" data-file-height="2534" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BT_Centre_3195_stitched.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The BT Centre was completed in 1985.</div></div></div>\n<p>BT Group\'s world headquarters and <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered office</a> is the <a href="/wiki/BT_Centre" title="BT Centre">BT Centre</a>, a 10-storey office building at 81 Newgate Street in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a>, opposite <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_tube_station" title="St. Paul&#39;s tube station">St. Paul\'s tube station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Buildings_and_stations">Buildings and stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Buildings and stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Some of its UK buildings and stations are:\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Adastral_Park" title="Adastral Park">Adastral Park</a> \xe2\x80\x93 headquarters of <a href="/wiki/BT_Research" title="BT Research">BT Labs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Suffolk" title="Suffolk">Suffolk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baynard_House,_London" title="Baynard House, London">Baynard House</a> \xe2\x80\x93 building in <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Riverside_Tower" title="BT Riverside Tower">BT Riverside Tower</a> \xe2\x80\x93 headquarters of BT Northern Ireland in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Tower_(Swansea)" title="BT Tower (Swansea)">BT Tower</a> - building in <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Goonhilly_Satellite_Earth_Station" title="Goonhilly Satellite Earth Station">Goonhilly Satellite Earth Station</a> operations center">network operations centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shropshire" title="Shropshire">Shropshire</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stadium_House,_Cardiff" title="Stadium House, Cardiff">Stadium House</a> \xe2\x80\x93 building in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a></li></ul></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications_towers">Telecommunications towers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Telecommunications towers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_towers_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Telecommunications towers in the United Kingdom">Telecommunications towers in the United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Telecom_microwave_network" title="British Telecom microwave network">British Telecom microwave network</a></div>\n<p>BT remains one of the largest owners of <a href="/wiki/Radio_masts_and_towers" title="Radio masts and towers">telecommunications towers</a> in the UK and were a major node in its <a href="/wiki/Microwave" title="Microwave">microwave</a> network. Its BT Tower in London is most notable for numerous reasons such as being the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of tallest buildings in the United Kingdom">tallest building in the UK</a> from its construction in the 1960s until the early 1980s, its <a href="/wiki/Revolving_restaurant" title="Revolving restaurant">revolving restaurant</a> at the top known as \'Top of the Tower\' in operation through the late 1960s and 1970s, and remains one of the UK\xe2\x80\x99s most important <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">communications</a> nerve centres, the heart of a vast <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting" title="Broadcasting">broadcasting</a> and communications network. It carries approximately 95% of the UK\'s TV content, including live broadcasts and 99% of all live football games as well as pinoneering the first international <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">HD</a>, <a href="/wiki/3D_television" title="3D television">3D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ultra-high-definition_television" title="Ultra-high-definition television">4K television</a> transmissions. It serves media production and distribution customers around the world and as part of the Things Connected Network launched in London, it became the highest building in the world to host an <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_things" title="Internet of things">Internet of Things</a> (IoT) <a href="/wiki/Base_station" title="Base station">base station</a> in September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Some of its towers are:\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/BT_Tower" title="BT Tower">BT Tower</a> in <a Tower">Tolsford Hill BT Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Turners_Hill_Transmitter" title="Turners Hill Transmitter">Turners Hill BT Tower</a> in <a Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gloucestershire" title="Gloucestershire">Gloucestershire</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Zouches_Farm_transmitting_station" title="Zouches Farm transmitting station">Zouches Farm</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bedfordshire" title="Bedfordshire">Bedfordshire</a></li></ul></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Groupbusinesses-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Customer_facing">Customer facing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span including:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/BT_Broadband" title="BT Broadband">BT Broadband</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_TV" title="BT TV">BT TV</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Mobile" title="BT Mobile">BT Mobile</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Wi-fi" title="BT Wi-fi">BT Wi-fi</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Business and Public Sector">BT Business and Public Sector</a> \xe2\x80\x93 provides retail telecoms and IT services to businesses and the public sector in the UK and Ireland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Global_Services" title="BT Global Services">BT Global Services</a> \xe2\x80\x93 provides telecoms and IT services to multinationals</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BT_Wholesale_and_Ventures" and Next Generation Text Service, services for media companies and broadcasters and its ventures side encompasses a portfolio of businesses offering a range of products and services</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Openreach" title="Openreach">Openreach</a> \xe2\x80\x93 fenced-off wholesale division, established in 2005 following a review by <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> and commenced operations in 2006, employing 25,000 engineers previously employed by BT. Its purpose is to ensure that other communications providers have the same operational conditions as BT, and is responsible for the provision and repair in the "<a href="/wiki/Last_mile" title="Last mile">last mile</a>" of copper wire.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_service_unit">Internal Openreach</li></ul></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pension_fund">Pension fund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Pension fund">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>BT has the largest <a href="/wiki/Defined_benefit_pension_plan" title="Defined benefit pension plan">defined benefit pension plan</a> of any UK public company.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The trustees valued the scheme at \xc2\xa336.7&#160;billion at the end of 2010;<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> an actuarial valuation valued the deficit of the scheme at \xc2\xa39.043&#160;billion as of 31 December 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\nFollowing a change in the regulations governing inflation index linking, the deficit was estimated at \xc2\xa35.2&#160;billion in November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-DeficitFall_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeficitFall-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sponsorships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Advert" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" width="40" height="40" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>contains content that is written like <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_soapbox_or_means_of_promotion" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">an advertisement</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by removing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Spam" title="Wikipedia:Spam">promotional content</a> and inappropriate <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">external links</a>, and by adding encyclopedic content written from a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutral point of view</a>.</span>  <small><i>(October 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>BT sponsored Scotland\'s domestic <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> championship and cup competitions between 1999 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-SRUSponsorship2014_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRUSponsorship2014-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 July 2012, it was announced that BT agreed a three-year sponsorship deal with <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Rugby" title="Ulster Rugby">Ulster Rugby</a> and sees BT become the Official Communications Partner. BT\'s logo will appear on the Ulster Rugby shirt sleeve for all friendlies, <a href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Pro12" title="2011\xe2\x80\x9312 Pro12">RaboDirect Pro12</a> matches as well as a significant brand presence at their home ground; <a href="/wiki/Ravenhill_Stadium" title="Ravenhill Stadium">Ravenhill Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 29 July 2013, it was announced that BT had partnered up with <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Rugby_Union" title="Scottish Rugby Union">Scottish Rugby Union</a> in a four-year sponsorship deal with its two professional clubs; <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Rugby" title="Edinburgh Rugby">Edinburgh Rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Warriors" title="Glasgow Warriors">Glasgow Warriors</a> that will commence from August 2013. The deal involves <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> becoming the new shirt sponsor for both clubs as well as being promoted with BT Group at their respective home grounds; <a href="/wiki/Scotstoun_Stadium" title="Scotstoun Stadium">Scotstoun Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Murrayfield_Stadium" title="Murrayfield Stadium">Murrayfield Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 May 2014, it was announced that BT agreed a \xc2\xa320 million four-year sponsorship deal with <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Rugby_Union" title="Scottish Rugby Union">Scottish Rugby Union</a> which includes BT securing the naming rights for <a href="/wiki/Murrayfield_Stadium" title="Murrayfield Stadium">Murrayfield Stadium</a> which becomes BT Murrayfield Stadium, become sponsor of the Scotland sevens team, become principal and exclusive sponsor of Scotland\'s domestic league and cup competitions from next season, taking over the role from <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Bank_of_Scotland_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="The Royal Bank of Scotland Group">The Royal Bank of Scotland Group</a> (RBS), and become sponsor of Scottish Rugby\'s four new academies that aims to drive forward standards for young players who have aspirations to play professionally.<sup id="cite_ref-SRUSponsorship2014_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRUSponsorship2014-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 April 2015, it was announced that as part of BT\'s current \xc2\xa320 million four-year sponsorship deal with <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Rugby_Union" title="Scottish Rugby Union">Scottish Rugby Union</a> that was announced in May 2014, BT has completed its sponsorship portfolio following an additional investment of \xc2\xa33.6 million for the 3 years remaining of its sponsorship deal, to become the new shirt sponsor for the Scotland national teams.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 January 2016, it was announced that BT, alongside <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> will be the new joint headline sponsors in a three-year deal with <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Television_Festival" title="Edinburgh International Television Festival">Edinburgh International Television Festival</a>. The two companies will "share prominence across all branding of the 41st TV Festival, including the famous <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Television_Festival#The_MacTaggart_Lecture" title="Edinburgh International Television Festival">MacTaggart Lecture</a> and will work closely with the festival organisers in their bid to reflect new trends in a rapidly transforming industry, from new ways of distributing content to technical innovations such as <a href="/wiki/Virtual_Reality" class="mw-redirect" title="Virtual Reality">Virtual Reality</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BT is the founding and principal partner of the <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> Foundation, which was established to improve the lives of children and young people. The Foundation will run events "to raise vital funds to support the work of key organisations dedicated to supporting disadvantaged and vulnerable children and young people". These organisations are four chosen charities which are, Manchester United Foundation, <a href="/wiki/National_Society_for_the_Prevention_of_Cruelty_to_Children" title="National Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Children">NSPCC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claire_House_Children%27s_Hospice" title="Claire House Children&#39;s Hospice">Claire House Children\'s Hospice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alder_Hey_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Alder Hey Children&#39;s Hospital">Alder Hey Children\'s Hospital</a>. The first of these events was Wayne\xe2\x80\x99s <a href="/wiki/Testimonial_match" title="Testimonial match">testimonial match</a> in August 2016 between <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton F.C.</a> which raised \xc2\xa31.2 million. The match was screened live through <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> with <a href="/wiki/BT_MyDonate" title="BT MyDonate">BT MyDonate</a> being the official fundraising platform for the testimonial, with both online and text options for donations promoted during the match.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 May 2017, it was announced that BT is to sponsor the 2017 <a href="/wiki/British_Urban_Film_Festival" title="British Urban Film Festival">British Urban Film Festival</a> (BUFF) and sees BT host every event of the film festival, including the Awards at the <a href="/wiki/BT_Tower" title="BT Tower">BT Tower</a>. BT will also broadcast the awards ceremony on BT.com and will have the opportunity to screen films acquired from the festival on its <a href="/wiki/BT_TV" title="BT TV">BT TV</a> store platform.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 September 2017, it was announced that BT had extended its current \xc2\xa320 million four-year sponsorship deal with <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Rugby_Union" title="Scottish Rugby Union">Scottish Rugby Union</a> that was announced in May 2014, for a further three years beginning from June 2018. The new deal sees BT retain the naming rights to <a href="/wiki/Murrayfield_Stadium" title="Murrayfield Stadium">BT Murrayfield Stadium</a>, alongside its role as principal partner of the Scotland national team and Scotland 7s. BT\'s logo will continue to be displayed on the front of Scotland rugby shirts across the world, in the <a href="/wiki/Six_Nations_Championship" title="Six Nations Championship">Six Nations Championship</a>, as well as the summer and autumn test matches. BT will also continue to be promoted at <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Rugby" title="Edinburgh Rugby">Edinburgh Rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotstoun_Stadium" title="Scotstoun Stadium">Scotstoun Stadium</a> in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_financial_performance">Historical financial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
