class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" width="45" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="354" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">The <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutrality</a> of this section is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">disputed</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:BT_Group##" title="Talk:BT Group">talk page</a>. Please do not remove this message until <a href="/wiki/Template:POV#When_to_remove" title="Template:POV">conditions to do so are met</a>.</span>  <small><i>(September 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 2004 the BT Group signed the world\'s largest renewable energy deal with <a href="/wiki/Npower_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Npower (UK)">npower</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centrica" title="Centrica">British Gas</a>, and now all of their exchanges, satellite networks and offices are powered by renewable energy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  BT is a member of the Corporate Leaders Group on Climate Change. They signed a letter urging the government to do more to tackle this problem. Janet Blake, head of global <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">corporate social responsibility</a> at BT, says that she would like to see incentives that find ways of rewarding those companies that focus on climate change by making investments in green business models.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BT has made it clear that it has an ambitious plan to reduce <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Its strategy includes steps to reduce the company\'s carbon footprint as well as those of customers, suppliers and employees. BT has pledged to achieve an 80% reduction by the year 2016, which will require further efficiency improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wide_Web_hyperlink_patent">World Wide Web hyperlink patent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: World Wide Web hyperlink patent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2001, BT discovered it owned a patent (<span><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US4873662">U.S. Patent 4,873,662</a></span>) which it believed gave it patent rights on the use of <a href="/wiki/Hyperlink" title="Hyperlink">hyperlink</a> technology on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>. The corresponding UK patent had already expired, but the US patent was valid until 2006. On 11 February 2002, BT began a court case relating to its claims in a US federal court against the <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service provider</a> <a href="/wiki/Prodigy_(ISP)" class="mw-redirect" title="Prodigy (ISP)">Prodigy Communications Corporation</a>.  In the case <i><a href="/wiki/British_Telecommunications_plc_v._Prodigy" title="British Telecommunications plc v. Prodigy">British Telecommunications plc v. Prodigy</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Southern_District_of_New_York" title="United States District Court for the Southern District of New York">United States District Court for the Southern District of New York</a> ruled on 22 August 2002 that the BT patent was not applicable to web technology and granted Prodigy\'s request for <a href="/wiki/Summary_judgment" title="Summary judgment">summary judgment</a> of non-infringement.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Behavioural_targeting">Behavioural targeting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Behavioural targeting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In early 2008 it was announced that BT had entered into a contract (along with <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media" title="Virgin Media">Virgin Media</a> and <a href="/wiki/TalkTalk_Group" title="TalkTalk Group">TalkTalk</a>) with the <a href="/wiki/Spyware" title="Spyware">spyware</a> company <a href="/wiki/Phorm" title="Phorm">Phorm</a> (responsible under their 121Media guise for the Apropos <a href="/wiki/Rootkit" title="Rootkit">rootkit</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> to intercept and analyse their users\' click-stream data and sell the anonymised aggregate information as part of Phorm\'s OIX advertising service.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The practice, known as "<a href="/wiki/Behavioural_targeting" class="mw-redirect" title="Behavioural targeting">behavioural targeting</a>" and condemned by critics as "data pimping", came under intense fire from various internet communities and other interested-parties who believe that the interception of data without the consent of users and web site owners is illegal under UK law (RIPA).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> At a more fundamental level, many have argued that the ISPs and Phorm have no right to sell a commodity (a user\'s data, and the copyrighted content of web sites) to which they have no claim of ownership. In response to questions about Phorm and the interception of data by the Webwise system Sir <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a>, credited as the creator of the World Wide Web protocol, indicated his disapproval of the concept and is quoted as saying of his data and web history:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It\'s mine \xe2\x80\x93 you can\'t have it. If you want to use it for something, then you have to negotiate with me. I have to agree, I have to understand what I\'m getting in return. I myself feel that it is very important that my ISP supplies internet to my house like the water company supplies water to my house. It supplies connectivity with no strings attached. My ISP doesn\'t control which websites I go to, it doesn\'t monitor which websites I go to.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Sir Tim Berners-Lee, 2008<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Huawei_infrastructure_access">Huawei infrastructure access</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Huawei infrastructure access">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Beginning in 2010 the UK intelligence community investigated <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a>, the Chinese supplier of BT\'s new fibre infrastructure with increasing urgency after the USA, Canada and Australia prevented the company from operating in their countries.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Although BT had notified the UK government in 2003 of Huawei\'s interest in their \xc2\xa310bn network upgrade contract, they did not raise the security implications as BT failed to explain that the Chinese company would have unfettered access to critical infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> On 16 December 2012 the prime minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> was supplied with an in-depth report indicating that the intelligence services had very grave doubts regarding Huawei, and that UK governmental, military, and civilian privacy may have been under serious threat.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 7 June 2013, British lawmakers concluded that BT should not have allowed Huawei access to the UK\'s communications network without ministerial oversight, saying they were \'deeply shocked\' that BT did not inform government that they were allowing Huawei and ZTE, both with ties to the Chinese military, unfettered access to critical national systems. Furthermore, ministers discovered that the agency with the responsibility to ensure Chinese equipment and code was threat-free was entirely staffed by Huawei employees. Subsequently, parliamentarians confirmed that in case of an attack on the UK there was nothing that could be done to stop Chinese infiltration.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 2016 Huawei had put measures in place to ensure the integrity of UK national security. Specifically their UK work is now overseen by a board that includes directors from <a href="/wiki/GCHQ" class="mw-redirect" title="GCHQ">GCHQ</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Office" title="Cabinet Office">Cabinet Office</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/ZTE" title="ZTE">ZTE</a>, another Chinese company that supplies extensive network equipment and subscriber hardware used with BT \xe2\x80\x98Infinity\xe2\x80\x99, was also under scrutiny by parliament\'s intelligence and security committee<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> after the US, Canada, Australia and the European Union declared the company a security risk.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_complicity_with_drone_strikes_in_Yemen_and_Somalia">Alleged complicity with drone strikes in Yemen and Somalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Alleged complicity with drone strikes in Yemen and Somalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In September 2012, BT entered into a $23 million deal with the US military to provide a key communications cable connecting <a href="/wiki/RAF_Croughton" title="RAF Croughton">RAF Croughton</a>, a US military base on UK soil, with <a href="/wiki/Camp_Lemonnier" title="Camp Lemonnier">Camp Lemonnier</a>, a large US base in Djibouti.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Camp Lemonnier is used as a base for American drone attacks in Yemen and Somalia, and has been described by <i>The Economist</i> as "the most important base for drone operations outside the war zone of Afghanistan."<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Human rights groups including <a href="/wiki/Reprieve_(organisation)" title="Reprieve (organisation)">Reprieve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> have criticised the use of armed drones outside declared war zones. Evidence produced by <a href="/wiki/The_Bureau_of_Investigative_Journalism" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bureau of Investigative Journalism">The Bureau of Investigative Journalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>\'s International Human Rights &amp; Conflict Resolution Clinic suggest that drone strikes have caused substantial civilian casualties, and may be illegal under international law.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, BT was the subject of a complaint by <a href="/wiki/Reprieve_(organisation)" title="Reprieve (organisation)">Reprieve</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Business,_Innovation_and_Skills" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Business, Innovation and Skills">Department of Business, Innovation and Skills</a> under the <a href="/wiki/OECD_Guidelines_for_Multinational_Enterprises" title="OECD Guidelines for Multinational Enterprises">OECD Guidelines for Multinational Enterprises</a>, following their refusal to explain whether or not their infrastructure was used to facilitate drone strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The subsequent refusal of this complaint was appealed in May 2014, on the basis that the UK National Contact Point\'s decision did not follow the OECD Guidelines. The issue of bias was also raised, due to the appointment of Lord Ian Livingston as government minister for the department which was processing the complaint: Livingston had occupied a senior position at BT when the cable between RAF Croughton and Camp Lemonnier was originally built.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BT_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"
